string = '6'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():
                try:
                    # Get our last two values
                    right = stack.pop()
                    left = stack.pop()
    
                    # Calculate and accumulate it
                    result = ops[character](left, right)
                    stack.push(result)
    
                # If there aren't enough operands, raise it.
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
            else:
                # Else it's either a number or garbage
                try:
                    # It'll raise an exception if it can't parse it.
                    value = int(character)
                    stack.push(value)
    
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
    
        # If we have too many operands or operators
        if stack.size == 1:
>           raise ValueError()
E           ValueError

stack1.py:131: ValueError

string = 'a"e{v#}1l$1\rqjR!'

    def check_parenthesis(string):
        stack = Stack()
        # We're using a dict which allows us to do some fun things!
        brackets = {'{':'}', '[':']', '(':')'}
    
        for character in string:
            # Keys being the left-side brackets
            if not character in brackets.keys():
                stack.push(character)
    
            # Values being the right-side brackets
            if character in brackets.values():

string = '6'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():
                try:
                    # Get our last two values
                    right = stack.pop()
                    left = stack.pop()
    
                    # Calculate and accumulate it
                    result = ops[character](left, right)
                    stack.push(result)
    
                # If there aren't enough operands, raise it.
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
            else:
                # Else it's either a number or garbage
                try:
                    # It'll raise an exception if it can't parse it.
                    value = int(character)
                    stack.push(value)
    
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
    
        # If we have too many operands or operators
        if not stack.size > 1:
>           raise ValueError()
E           ValueError

string = '/'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():

                    # Get our last two values
>                   right = stack.pop()

string = '(T lON)_'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():
                try:
                    # Get our last two values
                    right = stack.pop()
                    left = stack.pop()
    
                    # Calculate and accumulate it
                    result = ops[character](left, right)
                    stack.push(result)

                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e

                    stack.push(value)

string = 'Eo(l<,t{Sl=T`'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():
                try:
                    # Get our last two values
                    right = stack.pop()
                    left = stack.pop()
    
                    # Calculate and accumulate it
                    result = ops[character](left, right)
                    stack.push(result)
    
                # If there aren't enough operands, raise it.
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
            else:
                # Else it's either a number or garbage
                try:
                    # It'll raise an exception if it can't parse it.
                    value = int(character)
                    stack.push(value)

_ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ 

string = '3'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():
                try:
                    # Get our last two values
                    right = stack.pop()
                    left = stack.pop()
    
                    # Calculate and accumulate it
                    result = ops[character](left, right)
                    stack.push(result)
    
                # If there aren't enough operands, raise it.
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
            else:
                # Else it's either a number or garbage
                try:
                    # It'll raise an exception if it can't parse it.
                    value = int(character)
                    stack.push(value)
    
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
    
        # If we have too many operands or operators
        if stack.size > 1:
>           raise ValueError()
E           ValueError

string = '6'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():
                try:
                    # Get our last two values
                    right = stack.pop()
                    left = stack.pop()
    
                    # Calculate and accumulate it
                    result = ops[character](left, right)
                    stack.push(result)
    
                # If there aren't enough operands, raise it.
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
            else:
                # Else it's either a number or garbage
                try:
                    # It'll raise an exception if it can't parse it.
                    value = int(character)
                    stack.push(value)
    
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
    
        # If we have too many operands or operators
        if stack.size > 1:
>           raise ValueError()
E           ValueError

string = '6'

    def postfix_eval(string):
        ''' Here we setup a dictionary relating the characters of
            operations to lambda functions. It's similar to saying:
    
            def add(a,b):
                return a + b
    
            and then doing:
    
            print add(4,5)
            >>> 9
    
            The add function can also be accessed via the ``operator``
            module.
        '''
        stack = Stack()
        ops = {'+': lambda a, b: a + b,
               '-': lambda a, b: a - b,
               '*': lambda a, b: a * b,
               '/': lambda a, b: a / b,
               '%': lambda a, b: a % b,
               '^': lambda a, b: a ** b,}
    
        # Split the string into a list using spaces
        tokens = string.split(' ')
    
        for character in tokens:
            # Check if it's an operator
            if character in ops.keys():
                try:
                    # Get our last two values
                    right = stack.pop()
                    left = stack.pop()
    
                    # Calculate and accumulate it
                    result = ops[character](left, right)
                    stack.push(result)
    
                # If there aren't enough operands, raise it.
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
            else:
                # Else it's either a number or garbage
                try:
                    # It'll raise an exception if it can't parse it.
                    value = int(character)
                    stack.push(value)
    
                except ValueError as e:
                    raise e
    
        # If we have too many operands or operators
        if stack.size > 0:
>           raise ValueError()
E           ValueError
